    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText3215990869113352225" style="display:none"> Directors and executives of public corporations are dying in mysterious circumstances. <p>.Their only connection is irregular share dealings that took place in their companies before their deaths.</p><p>When young auditor, Todd Hansen, runs up a huge gambling debt with illegal bookies, he finds himself in serious trouble. The only way he can pay them is by providing confidential information about his firm’s corporate clients.</p><p>Caught, and sentenced to nine years in New York’s toughest prison, Todd is given a way out BUT it’s dangerous. There are those who think they’d be safer if he was dead.</p> Will a chance meeting with a Mafia boss in prison save Todd? <p> </p></span>

<div id="review_2392290881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2392290881" />
    <a title="No Shelf Control" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77684985-no-shelf-control"><img alt="No Shelf Control" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518444551p2/77684985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2392290881?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="No Shelf Control" class="user" itemprop="url" name="No Shelf Control" href="/user/show/77684985-no-shelf-control">No Shelf Control</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2392290881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13119106588149456590">Oh my goodness! This book surely got me reading like the “keeps going and going bunny” it was thaaat good! I mean, I seldom read novels of this caliber as I always pass them by but this book was given to me to review and wow! I could not put it down during the time I was reading it. It involves a group of white collar criminals who meet twice a month to discuss their illegal ways of acquiring money by way of blackmailing corporations and/or individuals who just happen to stumble upon bad luck an</span>
  <span id="freeText13119106588149456590" style="display:none">Oh my goodness! This book surely got me reading like the “keeps going and going bunny” it was thaaat good! I mean, I seldom read novels of this caliber as I always pass them by but this book was given to me to review and wow! I could not put it down during the time I was reading it. It involves a group of white collar criminals who meet twice a month to discuss their illegal ways of acquiring money by way of blackmailing corporations and/or individuals who just happen to stumble upon bad luck and/or unfortunate activities in life. These criminals included a former accountant, an engineer, a female former actuary, and a very dangerous gangster who liked to kill off his victims if he or she does not keep his or her promises. I don’t know if these doings are fictional or real but the thought of these type of people doing this to innocent, unsuspecting U.S. citizens makes me wish they are just make believe and not actually for real.<br /><br />Todd Hansen is the main character here who likes to take taxis to Chinatown to place bets on horse races. Eventually, he goes under the radar of those criminals I’ve mentioned above and ends up working for them. When his doings are caught he gets prison time but not without help from the FBI and his co-worker after he reveals to them who he has been working for. The FBI and his friend/co-worker assure him that he will be protected by a mafia boss already serving time in jail. When Todd is released he continues to work with the FBI to nail the bad men who work for the group of elite criminals that prey on people like him. I felt a soft-spot for Todd throughout the novel because he is innocent to the core and plus he had an obsession that got him in trouble in the first place. I do feel compassion for him and his friends Doug Lechte and Vanessa Hodge who all were targeted and hated by powerful colleagues and criminals alike who want to see them demoted or killed. It’s a great book and Ralph did an amazing job with it by filling it with a great and vast knowledge of the worlds of white collar crime, blackmail, and the FBI. I mean, I am impressed with his writing style and the first-hand experience he has in those mentioned I don’t think I can do the same if I am to write a similar-themed novel. It shows he has done his research very well. Kudos to him!<br /><br />I would definitely recommend this novel to old-school Sidney Sheldon fans like myself. I also would recommend this book to those who are looking for excitement in this month of May, where if you are planning to spend some time at the beach, at the pool, or in the comfort of your home, the characters and the plot of this book will surely entertain you and have you turning the pages over and over, eager to find out the outcome of all the shenanigans that this book embodies. From an avid reader to you, take my advice and order this book for yourself or your spouse now. The both of you will appreciate me for the recommendation. Good evening!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13119106588149456590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991902413?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth Birnbaum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth Birnbaum" href="/user/show/67534218-beth-birnbaum">Beth Birnbaum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991902413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13271036678744114716"><br/>                                    White Collar Blackmail<br/> <br/>            I thought White Collar Blackmail was going to be about some sort of genteel, cerebral crime, not quite a British drawing room mystery, but maybe close. I never expected a fast paced, action adventure full of surprises that would keep me wondering where it was heading until the very end, despite my usual ability to see a plot line coming.<br/> <br/>            I enjoy reading a book that is extremely well written, descriptive enough so </span>
  <span id="freeText13271036678744114716" style="display:none"><br />                                    White Collar Blackmail<br /> <br />            I thought White Collar Blackmail was going to be about some sort of genteel, cerebral crime, not quite a British drawing room mystery, but maybe close. I never expected a fast paced, action adventure full of surprises that would keep me wondering where it was heading until the very end, despite my usual ability to see a plot line coming.<br /> <br />            I enjoy reading a book that is extremely well written, descriptive enough so you can visualize everything going on, but with an economy of language that keeps the action flowing as you turn the page dying to know what’s going to happen next.  Sometimes the author gets in the way of his own story.  Peter J. Ralph does not.  He tells his story brilliantly.<br />           <br />            Some books require a character listing and their relationships.  White Collar Blackmail doesn’t.<br /> Although the book has good, good but flawed, and characters so bad you can’t help but hate them, you understand what made every one of them tick, memorable and distinct, and easy to keep track of.  <br /> <br />            White Collar Blackmail grabs you right in the Prologue.  The victims of supposedly random deaths all were vulnerable to blackmail.  One supposedly died of a heroin overdose, the other of kinky sex gone wrong, a third a degenerate gambler in massive debt supposedly in an accident.  What they have in common is that all of their companies were victims of major stock manipulation.  Naturally the international financial crime syndicate behind the murders needs to find their next victim, apparently they’re going through their patsys’ like a box of tissues.<br />           <br />            Todd Hansen, who created software he thinks he found a way to take the gambling out of horse racing so he can retire from accounting before he’s thirty, is targeted as the next victim.  The next thing Todd knows, his can’t miss system misses and he’s trapped into major losses.  Deeply in debt, he’s being blackmailed to commit insider trading to protect his family from being killed.  They aren’t gentle with him either.<br /> <br />            His love interest, Vanessa, is a hardworking accountant at Todd’s firm trying to make partner in spite of the managing partner thinking she isn’t blue blooded enough.  There are enough board machinations to keep a Dallas fan happy, and enough corporate criminal evil to make you think twice about buying stock.<br /> <br />            Family, the SEC, the FBI, a class war between the always had and the newly haves in Todd’s accounting firm, lots of information about stock manipulation that I actually understood, and outright psychotic, murderous criminals, all make for a wonderful read. I won't say more, no spoiler already here. Pick the book up, and you won't put it down.<br /> <br />           <br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13271036678744114716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2393218441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15083738184588399546">A corker of a thriller!<br/>I hadn't previously read any of Peter Ralph's novels before picking up 'White Collar Blackmail', but after this fast-pace cracker, I will definitely be reading more in the future. The plot is a compelling one and develops at an ever-increasing pace, right up to the shocking conclusion. Although the protagonist Todd Hansen is not the greatest of guys – a bit of a gambler, and mostly out for himself – I found myself rooting for him, even as he got himself into deeper and dee</span>
  <span id="freeText15083738184588399546" style="display:none">A corker of a thriller!<br />I hadn't previously read any of Peter Ralph's novels before picking up 'White Collar Blackmail', but after this fast-pace cracker, I will definitely be reading more in the future. The plot is a compelling one and develops at an ever-increasing pace, right up to the shocking conclusion. Although the protagonist Todd Hansen is not the greatest of guys – a bit of a gambler, and mostly out for himself – I found myself rooting for him, even as he got himself into deeper and deeper trouble. A gambling debt turns into a jail sentence, but it is about to get a whole lot worse. People want him dead, he has information that someone will go to extreme lengths to make sure it never gets out. Can the Mafia really be the ones to help him? Seems like a big risk to trust those that specialise in crime and dirty deeds.<br /><br />A gritty thriller that will keep you on the edge of your seat. The characters draw you into their stories and sub-plots, which are woven expertly into the main plot. A great read, that was a struggle to put down. I wonder what Peter Ralph novel to read next.<br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText5447166615009903509" style="display:none">White Collar Blackmail starts with three brutal murders. All high flying professionals, all linked to suspicious trade dealings. Why have these three been target for death, and how will low level finance worker Todd Hansen fit in? In the financial world, everyone should know to keep their mouths shut, especially when you work for a firm that deals with the finances of the rich and famous. Unfortunately, Todd has a little problem with gambling. To settle his debt, it's either find the money quick, go 'missing', or disclose company secrets. Prison follows and so does a chance to get out, but only if he puts himself in danger once again by getting in league with the Mafia. <br /><br />There is graphic violence, complex twists and turns, and characters that will confuse you as to whether they are good or bad, or even somewhere in the middle. How will things turn out for Todd? And will the big players in the financial world, let him get away with running his mouth? <br /><br /></span>

This is the first book I’ve read by Peter Ralph, but it certainly will not be the last. His ability to weave a believable story out of unbelievable events is simply fantastic.<br/><br/>There are numerous details in the plot, fine lines that tie everything together. Ralph is a master of keeping his story full and he doesn’t skip a beat when tying things together. I think my favorite part of this book is that it really throws u</span>
  <span id="freeText886928163801629240" style="display:none">From the very first chapter you can tell this book is going to be a page turner. This is the first book I’ve read by Peter Ralph, but it certainly will not be the last. His ability to weave a believable story out of unbelievable events is simply fantastic.<br /><br />There are numerous details in the plot, fine lines that tie everything together. Ralph is a master of keeping his story full and he doesn’t skip a beat when tying things together. I think my favorite part of this book is that it really throws us into a world that we don’t often get to see. Financial crimes are things we read about, but in this piece of fiction, we get to live and breathe it.<br /><br />Now, in the spirit of fairness I’ll say that the book could use a good edit, but don’t let that deter you. The story is well worth it for the complex plot, and I’m confident any books by this author will have the same attention to the story that this one had.<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13249043950738903242">White Collar Blackmail by Peter Ralph is a financial thriller that grabs your attention from the start. The main character Todd is a gambler and a good one. He has a flawless system that allows him to win big and to win fairly consistently. When his system ultimately fails, an organized group of white collar crooks raise his debt limit, further putting Todd into the hole. This unfortunately doesn't bode well for Todd the accountant. Todd is now in a huge mess, and must extricate himself somehow,</span>
  <span id="freeText13249043950738903242" style="display:none">White Collar Blackmail by Peter Ralph is a financial thriller that grabs your attention from the start. The main character Todd is a gambler and a good one. He has a flawless system that allows him to win big and to win fairly consistently. When his system ultimately fails, an organized group of white collar crooks raise his debt limit, further putting Todd into the hole. This unfortunately doesn't bode well for Todd the accountant. Todd is now in a huge mess, and must extricate himself somehow, someway. This is a riveting thriller, with an interesting cast of characters, and an all too real crime and scenario. With a fast pace, intricate plot, and intuitive writing style, this book is one that will keep you up at night until the well wrapped up ending. The author has done a great job in writing a cohesive, different style, financial thriller. Highly recommend.</span>

I don't want to give too much more of the plot away, as you should be as surprised as I was by the new developments.   <span id="freeText9253092657551615322" style="display:none">If you love crime thrillers like I do, then I recommend you pick up a copy of White Collar Blackmail, by Peter Ralph. It is interesting, exciting and so well-informed and researched – I could tell that parts of the plot had been developed from personal experience, which made it really believable and authentic. This book has a lot of dark themes, with blackmail, financial fraud, corporate espionage, and murder all crammed into this great piece of fiction. It was beautifully written from start to finish, with a great flow, and characters that evolved and developed throughout. It is gritty, dark and a totally addictive read. Definitely worth a 5 star rating. </span>

<div id="review_1424452313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424452313" />
    <a title="Mary Schecter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40276892-mary-schecter"><img alt="Mary Schecter" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424452313?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Schecter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Schecter" href="/user/show/40276892-mary-schecter">Mary Schecter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424452313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9911497808055917698">I’ve read several of Peter Ralph’s books, and I’ve enjoyed them, but with White Collar Blackmail I feel he’s developed his craft and produced a much more complex tale with some surprising twists and turns and a broad cast of characters. There are some truly evil people in this book, which I expected from him. There are some truly good people too, also expected. But here he delves deeper into his characters and shows us people with weaknesses who nevertheless find the courage to redeem themselves</span>
  <span id="freeText9911497808055917698" style="display:none">I’ve read several of Peter Ralph’s books, and I’ve enjoyed them, but with White Collar Blackmail I feel he’s developed his craft and produced a much more complex tale with some surprising twists and turns and a broad cast of characters. There are some truly evil people in this book, which I expected from him. There are some truly good people too, also expected. But here he delves deeper into his characters and shows us people with weaknesses who nevertheless find the courage to redeem themselves. There are also some violent criminals who sometimes behave fairly honorably. And he shows us sophisticated criminals who, as long as they stick to white collar crime, continue to be successful and evade the law, which fits what I’ve seen of the world. White Collar Blackmail is an untidy interweaving of various sorts of crime told in smooth, fast-paced scenes. A quick, entertaining read with some interesting insights into the devious use of labor unions, assorted corporate structures, and bank accounts. <br /><br />I received an advanced copy of this book for the purposes of review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9911497808055917698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

He begins to believe that possibly he can use this system to create a financial situation where he could quit his job and retire.   <span id="freeText13918861887625984229" style="display:none">Todd Hansen is an accountant obsessed with numbers and a system that he created. He has dabbled in betting on horseraces and finds that his system has been doing rather well. He begins to believe that possibly he can use this system to create a financial situation where he could quit his job and retire. When his system fails and allows Todd to suffer a few significant losses he becomes the mark of an organized group of white collar criminals. Their devious plan is to see to it that he is extended betting credit which will really get him in the hole. These criminals will pay his debt and use this to blackmail him into doing their bidding. Meanwhile authorities are investigating a string of suspicious deaths involving a senior executive of a corporation. Will Todd be able to get himself out of this mess before it is too late? Another well written and interesting book by Peter Ralph.<br />* I received an ARC of this book in exchange for an honest review. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yLc/CPFdz0d1py4W4r2QU3+/8vB3n+zxBPK7AuUtupVHo1gLGpzhDACPE6mbhxYluOi/KFCsaXXWJxX59e54jA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PQ7KIlLyfCb1UhYesa0fyZPxlwvLEN+iuyYgZZ2i93qyGq0huTNSbYB6K6HIl5m/VKba0+wjWiZp846ejWE1Yw==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer18221565913703677129">Peter Ralph is a former ‘big four’ chartered accountant who specialized in corporate reconstructions, recoveries, and liquidations. In the reconstructions, he acted as a surgeon chopping away the excess fat. In the recoveries, he was like a lifeguard giving mouth to mouth. In the liquidations, he was a combination of funeral director and forensic investigator.<br/> <br/>As a forensic investigator, Peter spe</span>
  <span id="freeText18221565913703677129" style="display:none">Peter Ralph is a former ‘big four’ chartered accountant who specialized in corporate reconstructions, recoveries, and liquidations. In the reconstructions, he acted as a surgeon chopping away the excess fat. In the recoveries, he was like a lifeguard giving mouth to mouth. In the liquidations, he was a combination of funeral director and forensic investigator.<br /> <br />As a forensic investigator, Peter spent a large part of his career investigating the reasons for corporate collapses and testifying in the courts.<br /><br />Later he became CEO of one of his recovery clients, a heavy transport equipment designer, and manufacturer that he successfully floated as a public company. <br /><br />He has a background well suited to writing financial thrillers. In 2012, he was highly commended in the Fellowship of Australian Writers National Literary Awards, for his novel about unconventional gas, Dirty Fracking Business.<br /><br />Sign up to his mailing list to receive FREE books and other promotions <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.peterralphbooks.com">http://www.peterralphbooks.com</a><br /><br />Follow him on: <br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/PeterRalphBooks">https://www.facebook.com/PeterRalphBooks</a><br />Twitter: @PeterRalphBooks</span>
  <a data-text-id="18221565913703677129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
